<span id="freeTextContainer929586111252724288">There is peril beneath the watchful eyes of the Lady...<br /><br />When Anna Pigeon left New York City after her husband was killed, she hoped it would be forever. But now her sister Molly is clinging to life in an uptown hospital ICU, so Anna has reluctantly returned. Rooming with a friend and fellow park ranger in close quarters on Liberty Island---the small strip of land that is ho</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText929586111252724288">There is peril beneath the watchful eyes of the Lady...<br /><br />When Anna Pigeon left New York City after her husband was killed, she hoped it would be forever. But now her sister Molly is clinging to life in an uptown hospital ICU, so Anna has reluctantly returned. Rooming with a friend and fellow park ranger in close quarters on Liberty Island---the small strip of land that is home to Lady Liberty---Anna spends her free time exploring the grand monument and the crumbling, overgrown, and eerie ruins in the unrestored sections of nearby Ellis Island. But the peace she seeks here is shattered when she finds herself among a crowd gathered at the Lady's base, staring at the broken body of a teenager who fell---or was pushed---to her death.<br /><br />The reason behind the youthful girl's fatal plunge is not the only mystery alive on these historic sites---nor will hers be the only death. Hidden in a dangerous labyrinth of stone, glass, and steel are secrets Anna Pigeon is now compelled to uncover...and an insidious threat to herself and to others that could wreak havoc on a nation's proudest day. There is peril beneath the watchful eyes of the Lady...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="929586111252724288">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1424576928">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424576928" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10665178-sara" class="left imgcol" title="Sara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451449917p2/10665178.jpg" alt="Sara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1424576928?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10665178-sara" class="user" title="Sara">Sara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8042019-liberty-falling" title="Paperback 9780425237359" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10665178-sara?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10665178-sara?shelf=novels-and-shorts" class="actionLinkLite">novels-and-shorts</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10665178-sara?shelf=series-i-need-to-finish" class="actionLinkLite">series-i-need-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1424576928">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer596374664534503768">For me, this was the best Anna Pigeon novel so far. She gets to see Molly - in not so good circumstances, she gets to see some guys (new and old), and best of all - she wanders all over the abandoned buildings at Ellis Island. That was the best thing about the book. Sure, there's the usual murder plot, but I liked the setting immensely.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_859011492">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859011492" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1910836-lobstergirl" class="left imgcol" title="Lobstergirl"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1380256801p2/1910836.jpg" alt="Lobstergirl" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/859011492?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1910836-lobstergirl" class="user" title="Lobstergirl">Lobstergirl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2163833.Liberty_Falling" title="Hardcover 9780399144592" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">admirers of Persian porn</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1910836-lobstergirl?shelf=mystery-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1910836-lobstergirl?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer859011492">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15925823374853194268">Absolutely horrendous writing, so thick with twisted metaphors that you have to reread sentences to find out what Barr is trying to say. The story is bad, too - the Liberty Island/Ellis Island setting is claustrophobic, the denouement dimwitted. Frederick Stanton, who used to be Anna's love interest but is now head over heels for the older, apparently homelier, and much unhealthier Molly, Anna's sister, is gross.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150420028" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/776067-karen" class="left imgcol" title="Karen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1200191220p2/776067.jpg" alt="Karen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/150420028?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 24, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/776067-karen" class="user" title="Karen">Karen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer150420028">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer457639973406144913">I don't usually like mysteries, but these Anna Pigeon books by Nevada Barr have captured me! Really, they are the first books I've read in a very long time that have me thinking about them even when I'm not reading: trying to figure out the solution to the mystery, or cogitating on Anna's unique and elegant way of reading others' body language, thoughts and feelings. Barr has an uncanny ability to evoke the sights, sounds, smells and feelings of our National Parks: wolves on Isle Royale, rafting</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText457639973406144913">I don't usually like mysteries, but these Anna Pigeon books by Nevada Barr have captured me! Really, they are the first books I've read in a very long time that have me thinking about them even when I'm not reading: trying to figure out the solution to the mystery, or cogitating on Anna's unique and elegant way of reading others' body language, thoughts and feelings. Barr has an uncanny ability to evoke the sights, sounds, smells and feelings of our National Parks: wolves on Isle Royale, rafting down the Rio Grande, or clambering around the ruins of Ellis Island. Occasionally Barr's prose gets a little convoluted and too rich in twisty metaphors, but that is easily forgiven when enjoying these fabulous thrillers.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="457639973406144913">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1235214430">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1235214430" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10358696-g-g" class="left imgcol" title="G.G."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442633588p2/10358696.jpg" alt="G.G." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1235214430?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10358696-g-g" class="user" title="G.G.">G.G.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1235214430">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13880373284732850057">Reports of ghostly sounds by the night Park Ranger on Ellis Island has Anna searching the historic landmark’s creepy abandoned buildings. But what has brought her to New York City is her sister’s illness. It’s a heart-wrenching time for Anna in what is one of Barr’s best stories.<br /><br />In Liberty Falling Barr reached a comfortable place writing Anna, the park ranger who grapples with murder in every park she works. The nice thing about this series is that Anna is such an authentic person, er, character</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13880373284732850057">Reports of ghostly sounds by the night Park Ranger on Ellis Island has Anna searching the historic landmark’s creepy abandoned buildings. But what has brought her to New York City is her sister’s illness. It’s a heart-wrenching time for Anna in what is one of Barr’s best stories.<br /><br />In Liberty Falling Barr reached a comfortable place writing Anna, the park ranger who grapples with murder in every park she works. The nice thing about this series is that Anna is such an authentic person, er, character. We like her because she screws up. She battles alcoholism, she struggles to express her feelings and she knows who we are because she is us. It’s the perfect combination of human weakness quelled by the strength we all somehow muster in challenging times.<br /><br />To be close to her sister, Anna’s staying at a friend’s house on Liberty Island. When a fourteen-year-old girl takes the express route down the Statue of Liberty—usually 354 claustrophobic steps and a hot two-hour climb—Anna’s attention is diverted from her sister. A visitor to the statue claims that a park employee pushed the dead girl. Anna likes the accused, in spite of knowing Hatch for only a short while, and can’t help doing a little investigating on her on even though she has no legal authority. When Hatch is found dead at the base of Lady Liberty some herald it as a guilt-induced suicide but Anna thinks it may be murder.<br /><br />Missing the open spaces in her home park of Mesa Verde, Colorado, Anna goes exploring Ellis Island, part of Liberty State Park. One building has been painstakingly restored to its lavish 1920s design but the others remain sad ruins of another era. During its day, 10,000 of the masses passed through Ellis Island each day hoping for a new beginning. The building consisted of a huge immigration center and state-of-the-art (at the time) hospital including operating theaters and autopsy facility. Today, the same numbers visit the compound and wonder what it must have been like. You will too because Barr describes it well and you almost feel lost in time.<br /><br />What she finds leads to a conspiracy of death and destruction if Anna can’t uncover who is behind it. In the final spellbinding pages Anna attempts to thwart a pernicious plot at Liberty’s feet in Barr’s shining homage to the best and worst of humankind.<br /><br />Liberty Falling does not fall short of expectations and instills in the reader a new appreciation for those who came before—yearning to breathe free.<br /><br />To read full review, go to: <a rel="nofollow" href="https://reluctantmediumatlarge.wordpress.com/?s=nevada+barr" target="_blank">https://reluctantmediumatlarge.wordpr...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13880373284732850057">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/3409675-nelda" class="left imgcol" title="Nelda"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Nelda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/902900545?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3409675-nelda" class="user" title="Nelda">Nelda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer902900545">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6457497503794672782">I was intrigued by the idea of novels written by a former Park Ranger and set in National Parks after reading about Nevada Barr's novels in the companion book to the PBS series about the history of the National Parks. My first read was set in Yosemite, and it was reasonably entertaining but had some flaws. The major interest for me was in the setting. Although I've not been to Yosemite yet, I did visit King's Canyon and Sequoia last year and they are near to Yosemite. While not wholly satisfied,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6457497503794672782">I was intrigued by the idea of novels written by a former Park Ranger and set in National Parks after reading about Nevada Barr's novels in the companion book to the PBS series about the history of the National Parks. My first read was set in Yosemite, and it was reasonably entertaining but had some flaws. The major interest for me was in the setting. Although I've not been to Yosemite yet, I did visit King's Canyon and Sequoia last year and they are near to Yosemite. While not wholly satisfied, I felt that the author deserved a second shot so I tried again with Liberty Falling.<br /><br />While I did enjoy the details about the parks featured in Liberty Falling (Liberty Island and Ellis Island), which were especially interesting since I had visited them in 2007, I have to say that I'm now done with this series and this writer. The writing is just not as strong as it needs to be for me to go any further. Characters are limited in scope and the whole plot is very formulaic. The primary focus of this writer seems to be in describing the strange interior life of this evidently resourceful but not very interesting woman, who happens to be a Park Ranger and happens to run into evil criminal activities, unpleasant coworkers, and too obviously suspicious characters at every turn - yawn. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6457497503794672782">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer929280553">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1110007560520007779">2.75 Stars This by far was not the best or strongest book in the Anna Pigeon series. I had heard some negative things about it and put off reading it as a result. I don't know if it was that Anna was out of her element being in NYC where she has gone to visit her sister who is in critical condition in the hospital. The book starts off slow with very little dialogue. There is a lot of internal angst going on with Anna throughout the book. Hidden in there is a mystery to be solved. There are death</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1110007560520007779">2.75 Stars This by far was not the best or strongest book in the Anna Pigeon series. I had heard some negative things about it and put off reading it as a result. I don't know if it was that Anna was out of her element being in NYC where she has gone to visit her sister who is in critical condition in the hospital. The book starts off slow with very little dialogue. There is a lot of internal angst going on with Anna throughout the book. Hidden in there is a mystery to be solved. There are deaths that occur at the Statue of Liberty, and Anna is determined to find out what has happened. There are relationship issues that get worked out amongst some of the series characters, so this is an important book to the series. Just don't start here. The series is much stronger than this entry, and I look forward to reading the next one.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1391269284">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391269284" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1994638-holly" class="left imgcol" title="Holly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1234016581p2/1994638.jpg" alt="Holly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1391269284?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 13, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1994638-holly" class="user" title="Holly">Holly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1994638-holly?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1994638-holly?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1391269284">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14722520354952462923">Anna Pigeon mystery #7 takes place in the National Park of NYC-Gateways Park, which encompasses Ellis Island and the Statue of Liberty. Anna has gone to NY to be with her sister Molly who is seriously ill. While she bunking with a park-ranger friend a teenage girl falls to her death at statue of liberty and the security guard who some say pushed her is found dead soon after.Interesting perspective- imagine living on Ellis Island with a view of Lady Liberty and the Manhattan skyline. Barr does a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14722520354952462923">Anna Pigeon mystery #7 takes place in the National Park of NYC-Gateways Park, which encompasses Ellis Island and the Statue of Liberty. Anna has gone to NY to be with her sister Molly who is seriously ill. While she bunking with a park-ranger friend a teenage girl falls to her death at statue of liberty and the security guard who some say pushed her is found dead soon after.Interesting perspective- imagine living on Ellis Island with a view of Lady Liberty and the Manhattan skyline. Barr does a good job of painting a vivid picture of the hospitals, morgue etc. on the island.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16822428260738768229">I have no idea when or where I got this book. Probably a yardsale, but it doesn't seem like the kind of book I would normally pick up. Maybe an old roommate left it? For a long time it was on my "unlikely to read" shelf, but because I'm a lamer, I hate to give away or sell a book that I haven't read... what if it turns out to be the best book I've ever read?!<br /><br />And so, I finally read this one. It helped that it fit a challenge for this quarter :P <br /><br />And then I immediately donated it to the reading lib</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16822428260738768229">I have no idea when or where I got this book. Probably a yardsale, but it doesn't seem like the kind of book I would normally pick up. Maybe an old roommate left it? For a long time it was on my "unlikely to read" shelf, but because I'm a lamer, I hate to give away or sell a book that I haven't read... what if it turns out to be the best book I've ever read?!<br /><br />And so, I finally read this one. It helped that it fit a challenge for this quarter :P <br /><br />And then I immediately donated it to the reading library in the hotel we were staying at in Lubec, Maine in exchange for <a title="One Day by David Nicholls" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6280118.One_Day">One Day</a>, which I'm excited to read ... eventually. We'll see how long it takes me to get to it.<br /><br />Aaaanyway, I really could have just gotten rid of this one. It was a quick, easy read, and helped me get points for my challenge, but those were just about the only redeeming qualities. The writing was atrocious (incredibly repetitive, and I really felt like there were paragraphs or scenes missing at times and I had to jump to lots of conclusions about what had happened, but there were no missing pages or other obvious things), the characters were unlikeable and the dialogue was just plain annoying. There seemed to be about 10 mysteries going on all at once, which just felt incredibly unrealistic. Sure, many of them ended up being related, but I also didn't feel like the resolution made any sense at all either. And the whole situation with the doctor that Anna was dating <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[turns out he was very much into pornography and photographing women naked, and the confusion over his internet search for "persian kittens" sex videos being confused with the interest over the actual Persian kitten (yes, a cat) that her sister had <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was just stupid and didn't add to the plot at all.<br /><br />I won't be reading any more of this series (probably, unless it fits another challenge, hah!).<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_70514404">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/70514404?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 08, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2606160-chris" class="user" title="chris">chris</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2606160-chris?shelf=anna-pigeon" class="actionLinkLite">anna-pigeon</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer70514404">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13435465105215076402">Tenacious park ranger Anna Pigeon leaves the country wilderness for the wilds of New York City, where her sister Molly is hospitalized, in this seventh installment of Barr's popular series (Blind Descent, etc.). Although Anna is on leave, she gets involved in the investigation of two murders. An unidentified child falls to her death from the Statue of Liberty. The main suspect dies. Anna is attacked. An actress is fatally bludgeoned on Ellis Island. Anna's conviction that these events are connec</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13435465105215076402">Tenacious park ranger Anna Pigeon leaves the country wilderness for the wilds of New York City, where her sister Molly is hospitalized, in this seventh installment of Barr's popular series (Blind Descent, etc.). Although Anna is on leave, she gets involved in the investigation of two murders. An unidentified child falls to her death from the Statue of Liberty. The main suspect dies. Anna is attacked. An actress is fatally bludgeoned on Ellis Island. Anna's conviction that these events are connected leads to a cross-country search for a right-wing fanatic. As expected with Barr, the narrative teems with memorable characters-among them Charlie DeLeo, the caretaker of the Statue of Liberty's torch, and Anna's former lover, FBI Agent Frederick Stanton, now smitten with Molly. Though Barr ties up the many subplots in an action-packed finale, the mystery is slow to develop and there's little doubt that Molly will recover. Barr's atmospherics remain potent, however. Her evocation of the isolated, exotic nature of the two famous tourist attractions is a particular treat, bringing home how nature is inexorably reclaiming buildings and records a stone's throw from bustling Manhattan.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13435465105215076402">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_457217349">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457217349" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2465614-c" class="left imgcol" title="C"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1327009996p2/2465614.jpg" alt="C" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/457217349?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2465614-c" class="user" title="C">C</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer457217349">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12020010350745127196">Strongly recommend checking out the Flickr photostream for Ellis Island. While Nevada Barr writes with excellent imagery, it's wonderful to be able to see what she's writing about. There's also a national geographic spread on the innards of the Statue of Liberty that is pretty nifty.<br /><br />I'm torn between 3 &amp; 4 on this. It did not rope me in as her past mysteries have (3), though I do enjoy her writing and there was much to like in this(4). There were a couple gruesome scenes that made eating a to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12020010350745127196">Strongly recommend checking out the Flickr photostream for Ellis Island. While Nevada Barr writes with excellent imagery, it's wonderful to be able to see what she's writing about. There's also a national geographic spread on the innards of the Statue of Liberty that is pretty nifty.<br /><br />I'm torn between 3 &amp; 4 on this. It did not rope me in as her past mysteries have (3), though I do enjoy her writing and there was much to like in this(4). There were a couple gruesome scenes that made eating a tomato-sauce based dinner an unusually unappetizing event (2). <br /><br />I loved the Ellis Island lore and the snapshot of NYC. I keenly felt Anna's claustrophobia in the city and the ache to get back to more open spaces. At the same time, I enjoyed the vicarious experience of the city's changed colors after dark and it made me homesick for nights back east when the air is, as she reflects, soft and warm and welcoming (except she leaves out the mosquitoes that come along with it...).<br /><br />Random observations:<br />In every book, there's a bitchy female character I want to punch in the face. These gals are as fixed a feature as Janet Evanovich's exploding cars. It makes me feel like Barr is working out some bad experiences with bullies in her past (which makes me wonder what Evanovich has against cars...). That, or the parks services are overflowing with angry young women itching to be nasty to each other.<br /><br />I have to admit that portraying - and slaying - these women in text is the perfect way to deal with them. She usually shows a grudging insight into the women's characters (mistreated, needy, low self esteem types) that makes me feel like I *should* empathize, but I usually don't. I don't exactly find myself cheering when one gets run over by a proverbial bus, granted, but it's more because I'd rather Anna was the bus rather than "fate" or "justice" (or the feds). I find myself torn between frustration and admiration at Anna's equanimity in the face of a slavering bully (and many other things). She doesn't walk away unaffected, but she doesn't retaliate or let people get a reaction out of her. While I wish I had that skill... a small part of me waits with baited breath for the day she trips someone and gives them a good shove. But, I have to say if she did, I'd lose some respect for her.<br /><br />There are a lot of great insights into human nature in these books, sometimes in general observation, more often in Anna's understanding of human behavior and her own reactions. I enjoy that. I often find myself relating to her desires to be away from people and out of the crush and her enjoyment of her solitude, while at the same time feeling a conflicting desire for company.<br /><br />One thing to note - it popped out at me when Anna corrected someone: <em>"Elk. There are no moose in Colorado."</em> Technically, there are, though not around Mesa Verde and Anna's home base in the SW corner of the state. Moose were introduced in North Park in the late 70's and have grown/spread since that time. They're frequently seen around Grand Lake and RMNP and, 13 years after the publication of the book, have wandered as far south as Pike National Forest SW of Denver. <br /><br />Random observations, spoiler edition:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<br />You find a drawer full of porn and a gym sock. So you pick up the gym sock and look inside? I don't care if there's only pictures in it, it's a sock in a porn filled desk drawer! That made me feel a little queasy.<br /><br />Persian Kittens... this cracked me up. First that Anna's cynical suspicious mind automatically went to real cats and not porn - of all the times for you to assume the best! And secondly, this is a reference to a real porn website with a similar name that was around in the 90's (and, given the first several pages of a google search results, is evidently still around). I loved Frederick's "you might want to look at that website..." The guy got it, of course. <br /><br />Frederick turns into such a smarmy doofus achieving even greater heights of dorkiness in the first 1/3 of the book than I even thought possible. He's nearly unbearable. "Molly, your sister is playing with dead people again." It felt like a total train wreck for a bit, especially when he started reading her sonnets. I was relieved when he got rid of what must have been a real bad case of nerves &amp; back to a little more...normal (well, as normal as Frederick gets).<br /><br />Also, I love that the bird owner bought his true love a 500$ cat...<br /><br />"The one ugly guard" lol<br /><br />I hope someone washed that ball cap before you stuck it on your head, Anna, someone's head got smashed inside it with their brains all oozing out and stuff. Since it was stolen out of evidence, one has to wonder. Porn socks and suicide hats, this is a novel with some seriously disturbing clothing.<br /><br />"Thanks for the drink and the talk. I think your son who just died might have been keeping a teen girl captive in your basement. Mind if I take a look?" <br /><br />"What are your plans for the Fourth of July?" Subtle hint, there, Ms. Barr. I'm so sad it was the one clue I figured out, too. Well, that and "that Mandy b@#$@ is up to no good." <br /><br />I love that she punched poor Dwight. I also loved the talking dumpster. <br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer269869623">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6308445314969240472">LIBERTY FALLING by Nevada Barr is 360 pages in paperback length. It is #8 in An Anna Pigeon Mystery.<br /><br />Brief Description:<br /><br />There is peril beneath the watchful eyes of the Lady...<br /><br />When Anna Pigeon left New York City after her husband was killed, she hoped it would be forever. But now her sister Molly is clinging to life in an uptown hospital ICU, so Anna has reluctantly returned. Rooming with a friend and fellow park ranger in close quarters on Liberty Island---the small strip of land that is home to L</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6308445314969240472">LIBERTY FALLING by Nevada Barr is 360 pages in paperback length. It is #8 in An Anna Pigeon Mystery.<br /><br />Brief Description:<br /><br />There is peril beneath the watchful eyes of the Lady...<br /><br />When Anna Pigeon left New York City after her husband was killed, she hoped it would be forever. But now her sister Molly is clinging to life in an uptown hospital ICU, so Anna has reluctantly returned. Rooming with a friend and fellow park ranger in close quarters on Liberty Island---the small strip of land that is home to Lady Liberty---Anna spends her free time exploring the grand monument and the crumbling, overgrown, and eerie ruins in the unrestored sections of nearby Ellis Island. But the peace she seeks here is shattered when she finds herself among a crowd gathered at the Lady's base, staring at the broken body of a teenager who fell---or was pushed---to her death.<br /><br />The reason behind the youthful girl's fatal plunge is not the only mystery alive on these historic sites---nor will hers be the only death. Hidden in a dangerous labyrinth of stone, glass, and steel are secrets Anna Pigeon is now compelled to uncover...and an insidious threat to herself and to others that could wreak havoc on a nation's proudest day.<br /><br />It had been a while since I had read the last book in this series, but once I started reading I started remembering what had been in the past. The descriptions of the Statue Of Liberty and the Island she stays on was very well done. I felt like I was right there and looking out through the crown. Even when Anna is riding the subway to get to the hospital to see her sister, Molly, you felt like you were on the streets of the city. <br /><br />In this book the alcoholism doesn't seem to be the focus as much as the sickness that could take Molly away from Anna. It was nice to see Anna get over Stanton and to let Molly be happy for a change. I do like the exchanges between Anna and Stanton though and I hope that in future books they will continue to work together. <br /><br />I am giving this 4 out of 5 stars as it did seem to be a little long and didn't seem to move fast until the very end. This was a book I could have let sit and not pick back up. <br /><br />BUY NOW: Conniesbookshelf.com $3.99</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/192020403?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 11, 2012</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer192020403">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14873840745325170903">"<em>There is peril beneath the watchful eyes of the Lady ...</em><br /><br />"When Anna Pigeon lift New York City after her husband was killed, she hoped it would be forever. But now her sister Molly is clinging to life in an uptown hospital ICU, so Anna has reluctantly returned. Rooming with a friend and fellow park ranger in close quarters on Liberty Island -- the small strip of land that is home to Lady Liberty -- Anna spends her free time exploring the grand monument and the crumbling, overgrown, and eerie ruin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14873840745325170903">"<em>There is peril beneath the watchful eyes of the Lady ...</em><br /><br />"When Anna Pigeon lift New York City after her husband was killed, she hoped it would be forever. But now her sister Molly is clinging to life in an uptown hospital ICU, so Anna has reluctantly returned. Rooming with a friend and fellow park ranger in close quarters on Liberty Island -- the small strip of land that is home to Lady Liberty -- Anna spends her free time exploring the grand monument and the crumbling, overgrown, and eerie ruins in the unrestored sections of nearby Ellis Island. But the peace she seeks here is shattered when she finds herself among a crowd gathered at the Lady's base, staring at the broken body of a teenager who fell -- or was pushed -- to her death.<br /><br />"The reason behind the young girl's fatal plunge is not the only mystery alive on these historic sites -- nor will hers be the only death. Hidden in a dangerous labyrinth of stone, glass, and steel are secrets Anna Pigeon is now compelled to uncover .. and an insidious threat to herself and to other that could wreak havoc on a nation's proudest day."<br />~~back cover<br /><br />I enjoyed the "tour" of Ellis Island, but was somewhat dismayed at the state of the buildings as portrayed in the book. Somehow, we should be able to do better for such an important part of our history &amp; heritage!<br /><br />Since I'm rereading this series to follow Anna's emotional progress, the situation with ex-boy friend FBI agent Frederick Stanton was pretty interesting to me (no spoilers here!)<br /><br />The plot was good, as usual -- convoluted, a bit more so -- each book seems to feature a more convoluted, less evident plot. This books was less dark than the last, although maybe the fact that it's set above ground skews my opinion about that.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12176252883399939441">If there’s anything that makes Anna more claustrophobic than Lechugilla Cave (Blind Descent), it’s a city. Not only are cities crowded with the living but they are also filled with memories of her long-mourned husband Zach. Her sister Molly is seriously ill though, hospitalized and in the Intensive Care Unit, so off to Manhattan Anna goes. When she arrives, her anxiety escalates when she discovers that Frederick Stanton is also in town: the same Frederick Stanton she was dating before he met and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12176252883399939441">If there’s anything that makes Anna more claustrophobic than Lechugilla Cave (Blind Descent), it’s a city. Not only are cities crowded with the living but they are also filled with memories of her long-mourned husband Zach. Her sister Molly is seriously ill though, hospitalized and in the Intensive Care Unit, so off to Manhattan Anna goes. When she arrives, her anxiety escalates when she discovers that Frederick Stanton is also in town: the same Frederick Stanton she was dating before he met and fell in love with her sister.<br /><br />When she’s not in the ICU, Anna escapes the crush of humanity by staying with a friend on Liberty Island. Exploring the abandoned structures on Ellis and Liberty Islands provides some way to work through her fears for Molly and her angst about Frederick. Of course, it also leads her into danger as she stumbles across evidence that something crooked is afoot. She suspects that everything ties together with the young girl who jumped–or was pushed–from the Statue of Liberty. Why would the girl take a nosedive from the monument? Why did someone take her backpack immediately after she fell? Why has no one claimed her body? Why is one security guard so obsessed with the incident?<br /><br />Solid, well-plotted mystery; interesting characters. Fascinating behind-the-scenes look at areas of Liberty and Ellis islands that are off-limits to tourists: I loved the eerie otherworldiness of the abandoned structures gradually being reclaimed by nature.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14241222591514986662">I think I like Anna Pigeon better in the wilds of her other assignments. I also like when she's actually working in the wilds of her other assignments. Anna, in this one, is in New York to look after her sister who is in the ICU in an uptown hospital.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=pc" class="actionLinkLite">pc</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=read-in-2012" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer25781363">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17387772893737749293">Liberty Falling by Nevada Barr is the seventh in the Anna Pigeon mystery series. It is set in New York City, Liberty Island and Ellis Island. Anna is there because her sister is in intensive care. When she's not working as a park ranger, she's sitting at her sister's bedside in the hospital.<br /><br />Anna, though, is preoccupied at work by two very similar deaths at the Statue of Liberty. Her anger over both of them, combined with her sister's ill health put her in a very poor and self destructive mood al</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17387772893737749293">Liberty Falling by Nevada Barr is the seventh in the Anna Pigeon mystery series. It is set in New York City, Liberty Island and Ellis Island. Anna is there because her sister is in intensive care. When she's not working as a park ranger, she's sitting at her sister's bedside in the hospital.<br /><br />Anna, though, is preoccupied at work by two very similar deaths at the Statue of Liberty. Her anger over both of them, combined with her sister's ill health put her in a very poor and self destructive mood all the way through.<br /><br />She spends her late nights exploring the ruins of Ellis Island, often putting herself in danger from the poor repair of the structures. While I normally love following along as a character explores old, crumbling buildings, I felt a disconnect here that just pulled me out of the story. Part of that disconnect was the realization that fictional Anna was there at the same time my family and I were there. The other part, stemmed from Anna's own recklessness — going at night without a partner, no ropes or other safety equipment.<br /><br />Finally, there's the mystery itself. Once all of Anna's anger and self destruction is pushed aside, the actual who done it and why is pretty basic. I think for this volume of the series, too much time was spent on character development at the cost of the mystery. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17387772893737749293">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5331165145979627389">I have not personally visited Ellis Island, but feel like I have a great concept of the layout. Nevada Barr did a great job of allowing the reader to get a feeling of where they were, where Ms. Pigeon was going and feeling and setting the tone for the entire story. It was hard to stop reading when you knew something else was going to arise. <br /><br />I'm sure this is part of a series. While the book could stand alone, I felt like I had missed out on pieces of Anna's back-story. Beyond that, the story mesh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5331165145979627389">I have not personally visited Ellis Island, but feel like I have a great concept of the layout. Nevada Barr did a great job of allowing the reader to get a feeling of where they were, where Ms. Pigeon was going and feeling and setting the tone for the entire story. It was hard to stop reading when you knew something else was going to arise. <br /><br />I'm sure this is part of a series. While the book could stand alone, I felt like I had missed out on pieces of Anna's back-story. Beyond that, the story meshed well. In many ways, I could almost have skipped everything to do with Anna's sister. I didn't feel like it added much to the overall story - more of a filler to make a page quota. Parts of it were needed, to give Anna a reason to be in the city and to establish connections.<br /><br />As someone who enjoys mysteries, this was a good book and one I would recommend to others.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8963507121905659421">Generally, I like her work. Plus the feeling that she is just a visitor, not in place as a park official also takes away from the feeling that this is an official Nevada Barr novel.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1031794546">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3404215277811435931">Anna Pigeon's adventure moves out of the wilderness and into the Big City, proving this author's talent at evoking a connection to the places she writes about is not limited to the great outdoors.<br /><br />If you love creepy old buildings, history and mystery you will enjoy this dance in the concrete jungle, twisted through Ellis and Liberty Islands. <br /><br />I can usually figure out the Anna Pigeon plots, but this one kept me in the dark right up till the end. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer668820583">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9187618779161161439">Though she typically eschews the city (or at least, has for the past few decades), Anna finds herself back in NYC to worry over her sister, who's in the ICU. Who does she find there but Frederick Stanton, of course?<br />To avoid Stanton, Anna tries to stay out of the way at Ellis and Liberty islands, where she's bunking with Patsy Silva and a grouchy housemate. Anna retreats to the ruins of Ellis and to the Statue at night, where she befriends a few security rangers. But where Anna goes, trouble cann</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9187618779161161439">Though she typically eschews the city (or at least, has for the past few decades), Anna finds herself back in NYC to worry over her sister, who's in the ICU. Who does she find there but Frederick Stanton, of course?<br />To avoid Stanton, Anna tries to stay out of the way at Ellis and Liberty islands, where she's bunking with Patsy Silva and a grouchy housemate. Anna retreats to the ruins of Ellis and to the Statue at night, where she befriends a few security rangers. But where Anna goes, trouble cannot be far behind, and soon there's one body, and then two.<br />Nothing is simple to Anna, and she feels certain that the various deaths and misdemeanors she hears about (or experiences) must be somehow connected. And in the end, we learn that when a handful of crimes seem like they ought to be connected, one must look for an even bigger crime to cover them all. I look forward to visiting Liberty and Ellis after reading this book.</span>

        <a href="/review/show/126007783?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4380068-bill" class="user" title="Bill">Bill</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4380068-bill?shelf=mystery-us" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-us</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4380068-bill?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer126007783">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16522700294994056372">Another comfort read from Nevada Barr. In the 7th book in this excellent series, we find our intrepid National Park ranger, Anna Pigeon, on a leave of absence, in New York, watching over her psychologist sister, Molly, who is critically ill. Anna is staying with her friend Patsy who is the chief administrator at the national park on Liberty and Ellis Islands. Even though preoccupied with her sister's health, Anna finds herself embroiled in a mysterious death on Liberty Island. The story moves al</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16522700294994056372">Another comfort read from Nevada Barr. In the 7th book in this excellent series, we find our intrepid National Park ranger, Anna Pigeon, on a leave of absence, in New York, watching over her psychologist sister, Molly, who is critically ill. Anna is staying with her friend Patsy who is the chief administrator at the national park on Liberty and Ellis Islands. Even though preoccupied with her sister's health, Anna finds herself embroiled in a mysterious death on Liberty Island. The story moves along a nice pace, sometimes a bit slowly, as Anna moves between the hospital and her off-duty investigation of a young girl's death, presumed suicide. Nevada Barr knows how to string along a neat mystery and to build the tension to an exciting climax. Always entertaining to read, I enjoyed this latest installment and look forward to visiting with Anna soon to see what new National Park will find her embroiled in a mystery.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16522700294994056372">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer107088133">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12525012855583232498">Series mysteries are a challenge. To read, because after a while they can't help but being, even in the hands of the most skilled writer, somewhat repetitious, and they have to be a struggle to write, at least after 3 or 4 of them. I bet Sue Grafton wishes the alphabet had fewer letters!<br /><br />Nevertheless, of all the Anna Pigeons I've read Liberty Falling is the one that is the most memorable. I know I've clean forgotten some of them. Perhaps it's the sub-plot of the sick sister, that adds a touch of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12525012855583232498">Series mysteries are a challenge. To read, because after a while they can't help but being, even in the hands of the most skilled writer, somewhat repetitious, and they have to be a struggle to write, at least after 3 or 4 of them. I bet Sue Grafton wishes the alphabet had fewer letters!<br /><br />Nevertheless, of all the Anna Pigeons I've read Liberty Falling is the one that is the most memorable. I know I've clean forgotten some of them. Perhaps it's the sub-plot of the sick sister, that adds a touch of complexity, also her descriptions of the Ellis Island ruins were haunting. I'm from NYC and my father went though Ellis Island as did the parents of many of my friends and I found I knew very little of it's history or it's present state.<br /><br />As I volunteer for the Park Service I didn't even know Ellis Island was part of it. A really good read. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13909360930960485879">This was the first of the Anna Pigeon series I've read, and I was really caught up in the characters. Some reviewers disliked how the author dwelt on the sister and the ex, but I enjoyed it as backstory. Other mysteries in the series are a little tighter, but this one was enjoyable enough to get me hooked on Barr's writing.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mHvxTpzJGEoDlCCwsqkHU1Y00gQyKQqwFpUpJMirvn/9r86dbhsMsI9MVAvMyOHhH8MRHXv0TRp8nCy2BD5IOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/43613.Nevada_Barr">About Nevada Barr</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/43613.Nevada_Barr"><img alt="43613" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1251393185p2/43613.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer17111477275207254280">Nevada Barr is a mystery fiction author, known for her "Anna Pigeon" series of mysteries, set in National Parks in the United States. Barr has won an Agatha Award for best first novel for Track of the Cat.<br /><br />Barr was named after the state of her birth. She grew up in Johnstonville, California. She finished college at the University of California, Irvine. Originally, Barr started to pursue a career in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17111477275207254280">Nevada Barr is a mystery fiction author, known for her "Anna Pigeon" series of mysteries, set in National Parks in the United States. Barr has won an Agatha Award for best first novel for Track of the Cat.<br /><br />Barr was named after the state of her birth. She grew up in Johnstonville, California. She finished college at the University of California, Irvine. Originally, Barr started to pursue a career in theatre, but decided to be a park ranger. In 1984 she published her first novel, Bittersweet, a bleak lesbian historical novel set in the days of the Western frontier.<br /><br />While working in Guadalupe Mountains National Park, Barr created the Anna Pigeon series. Pigeon is a law enforcement officer with the United States National Park Service. Each book in the series takes place in a different National Park, where Pigeon solves a murder mystery, often related to natural resource issues. She is a satirical, witty woman whose icy exterior is broken down in each book by a hunky male to whom she is attracted (such as Rogelio).<br /><br />Currently, Ms. Barr lives in New Orleans, LA.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/nevadabarr" target="_blank">http://us.macmillan.com/author/nevada...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17111477275207254280">...more</a>

    </div>

This island paradise has secrets it would keep; not just in the present, but in shadows from its gritty past, when it served as a prison for the Lincoln conspirators during and after the Civil War.\n\nHere, on this last lick of the United States, in a giant crumbling fortress, Anna has little company except for the occasional sunburned tourist or unruly shrimper. When her sister, Molly, sends her a packet of letters from a great-great-aunt who lived at the fort with her husband, a career soldier, Anna\'s fantasy life is filled with visions of this long-ago time.\n\nWhen a mysterious boat explosion-and the discovery of unidentifiable body parts-keeps her anchored to the present, Anna finds crimes of past and present closing in on her. A tangled web that was woven before she arrived begins to threaten her sanity and her life. Cut off from the mainland by miles of water, poor phone service, and sketchy radio contact, and aided by one law-enforcement ranger, Anna must find answers or weather a storm to rival the hurricanes
